  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6c02cc06-47ff-4b6a-9936-49900d6a793c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText5106069552647206980" style="display:none"><div>Nancy Kington, daughter of a rich merchant, suddenly orphaned when her father dies, is sent to live on her family's plantation in Jamaica. Disgusted by the treatment of the slaves and her brother's willingness to marry her off, she and one of the slaves, Minerva, run away and join a band of pirates. <br /><br />For both girls the pirate life is their only chance for freedom in a society where both are treated like property, rather than individuals. Together they go in search of adventure, love, and a new life that breaks all restrictions of gender, race, and position. Told through Nancy's writings, their adventures will appeal to readers across the spectrum and around the world.</div></span>

<div id="review_118233043" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118233043" />
    <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess"><img alt="Cora Tea Party Princess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548255984p2/4166936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118233043?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cora Tea Party Princess" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess">Cora Tea Party Princess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118233043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15245770867379415025"><b>5 Words: Swashbuckling adventure. Love, danger, life.</b><br/><br/>I always find it so difficult to review my favourite books. I just can't put my feelings into words. It's particularly hard when I have read that book so many times over the past decade that the pages are falling out and the cover's peeling off, because by now my love for the book has no reason, it just is.<br/><br/>Pirates! is such an adventure. It has so many twists and turns and shocks and some really sweet and poignant moments. It's a book that sets</span>
  <span id="freeText15245770867379415025" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Swashbuckling adventure. Love, danger, life.</b><br /><br />I always find it so difficult to review my favourite books. I just can't put my feelings into words. It's particularly hard when I have read that book so many times over the past decade that the pages are falling out and the cover's peeling off, because by now my love for the book has no reason, it just is.<br /><br />Pirates! is such an adventure. It has so many twists and turns and shocks and some really sweet and poignant moments. It's a book that sets my heart racing, it's a book that has such a vivid world that I am lost to real life when I read it. It's dramatic and thought-provoking.<br /><br />Every time I read this book, I get more out of it than before. It's one of those books that I itch to read at least once a year and turn to when life's just getting too much. It's a safety blanket make of pure escapism.<br /><br />This book is wonderfully written, in a quirky style. I love the journey that Nancy takes, both physically and as a person.<br /><br />It's a book I can see clear as day when I close my eyes. It would make an amazing film or mini-series.<br /><br />Now that I'm kind of finished gushing (for now) I urge you to get out and grab a copy of this book and get stuck in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15245770867379415025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24048976?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/225957-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24048976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16101729093112039991">I know that this is supposed to be a fun little book, and I think the audience might be aimed at younger ages, but in the end, it felt inconsistent on so many levels that I was just left feeling confused and/or disappointed, depending upon the chapter.<br/><br/>For one, Rees seems to have done a good amount of research for this book, yet I felt that she wasted it every time she turned a blind eye to conventions of the day. I don't care how accurately you can describe various ships if you don't also think </span>
  <span id="freeText16101729093112039991" style="display:none">I know that this is supposed to be a fun little book, and I think the audience might be aimed at younger ages, but in the end, it felt inconsistent on so many levels that I was just left feeling confused and/or disappointed, depending upon the chapter.<br /><br />For one, Rees seems to have done a good amount of research for this book, yet I felt that she wasted it every time she turned a blind eye to conventions of the day. I don't care how accurately you can describe various ships if you don't also think that the impressive suntan one would get from working in the sun everyday in the Caribbean for months will be a problem once a lady tries to dress up pretty and mingle with society. And don't even get me started on the pacing. If the historical inconsistencies left me disappointed, the strangely anti-climactic resolutions to all the dramatic moments just left me scratching my head. <br /><br />The worst of Rees' crimes of inconsistency, though, was the juxtaposition of some pretty grisly scenes, all things considered, with the rosy view of pirate life, where all men are decent except when riled up by a few bad apples and their apparently magically demonic musical instruments. As for the love story, I'm just thankful it wasn't a major component. Boy and girl grow up together and naturally fall in love. Boy (16) leaves girl (12) for the sea. Over the next 8ish years, they see each other, oh, let's do the math for fun.<br />2 hours - talking in a stable<br />6 hours - ball in Bath<br />1 hour - girl is prisoner on boy's ship<br />____<br />9 hours. Yet we leave girl as she goes off to look for the only man she will ever marry. The only reason either of them are still so faithful is because they haven't managed a whole day together since they were pre-pubescent.<br /><br />Happily leaving the ship.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16101729093112039991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_289274982" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289274982" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289274982?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of historical (esp. pirate) fiction; action heroine fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=action-heroines">action-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289274982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10728138717870437961">Although I haven't read much pirate-themed fiction, I find the premise interesting; so I've had my eye on this historical novel ever since the BC library (where I work) acquired it. It definitely didn't disappoint! Set mostly in the early 1720s, with some stage-setting in the years leading up to those, this action-packed tale follows the life and adventures of first-person narrator Nancy Kington (b. ca. 1704), the daughter of a Bristol merchant, who finds herself packed off to the family's plant</span>
  <span id="freeText10728138717870437961" style="display:none">Although I haven't read much pirate-themed fiction, I find the premise interesting; so I've had my eye on this historical novel ever since the BC library (where I work) acquired it. It definitely didn't disappoint! Set mostly in the early 1720s, with some stage-setting in the years leading up to those, this action-packed tale follows the life and adventures of first-person narrator Nancy Kington (b. ca. 1704), the daughter of a Bristol merchant, who finds herself packed off to the family's plantation in Jamaica at the age of 15, and is subsequently led by circumstances to voluntarily sign articles on a pirate ship.<br /><br />Pirates, of course, are sea-going robbers; by definition, they forcibly steal other people's property for their own profit. Obviously, they're off of the ethical strait-and-narrow path, and in shady moral territory. The piratical profession most naturally appeals to brutal and self-serving types who don't have any particular moral sense or empathy with their fellow humans. (Some may be more brutal and selfish than others --and some spectacularly evil and sadistic types may find the pirate life an opportunity to gratify their propensities.) Like Robert Louis Stevenson before her, British writer Rees gives full recognition to that reality. To a greater extent than Stevenson, though, she recognizes that there can be a range of nuanced moral qualities among pirates, with not all of them quite fitting that model --especially in a time and place where patriarchy and male chauvinism, legalized slavery, and institutionalized inequality and injustice greatly constrict many people's lives and choices, and might render the right side of the law as morally dicey as life under the Jolly Roger. (That's not unlike the situation in the Old West, or in medieval Europe, where "outlaws" might sometimes be decent people pushed outside the law by others using the system for their own gain.) Personally, I think that pirates who aren't brutal and selfish as such, and who do have a strong moral sense and a concern for others, can be interesting characters in the ways they navigate the shades of grey that their position necessarily entails; and that's true of our heroine here. (Yes, a lady who happens to be a pirate can be an honorable and admirable heroine!)<br /><br />This is fiction in the Romantic tradition --that is, fiction that seeks primarily to evoke strong emotional responses from the reader, sometimes enhanced, as they are here, by extreme situations and exotic settings. The Romantic aim is fully fulfilled here; I was taken captive by this pirate right away, turned the pages as fast as I could at every opportunity, and experienced a wealth of complex emotions throughout the story. (It's not, however, a "romance novel" in the Harlequin sense --though it has clean romance as one strand of the plot, which I appreciated-- and it doesn't "romanticize" things like piracy, slavery, and the grim realities of ocean-going life in the 18th century). It's also fiction with serious food for thought, as well as rousing adventure, and a very moving portrait of cross-racial friendship. Like most modern Romantic fiction, though, it borrows Realist techniques, with a concern for verisimilitude and historical accuracy. (In common with some other authors, Rees used the contemporary nonfiction <i>A General History of the Robberies and Murders of the Most Notorious Pyrates</i>, which she and some others attribute to Daniel Defoe, as a key source.) Nancy's narrative voice is engaging and quick-flowing, with a slightly archaic flavor in word choices and diction for realism, but is much easier to read than an actual 18th-century narrative would have been. <br /><br />Born in 1949, former schoolteacher Rees is an accomplished novelist, the author of some 19 books, and a History major (she actually had a double major, but History was one). Her publishers market her books to the YA age group (and the BC library put this one in the Juvenile section on that account), in this case probably encouraged by the fact that Nancy and her friend and fellow pirate Miranda are in their teens. Bad language of the d-word sort is present but relatively restrained, rape or attempted rape and prostitution are part of their world but not portrayed in great detail, and while there are some very violent and grisly moments, Rees doesn't wallow in them. The content here, IMO, wouldn't be harmful to a healthy teen; and I could see plenty of teen readers of both sexes eating it up with a spoon and asking for more. But it could just as easily have been marketed as an adult novel; there isn't anything stereotypically juvenile or "kiddish" about it. (Teens in Nancy and Miranda's day were expected to grow up quickly, and our gals here definitely did --they have far more in common, in their capacities and general attitudes, with today's adult women than they do with typical modern teens.)<br /><br />This particular edition of the book has a moderately interesting interview with the author (originally published in a Michigan newspaper), and a few pages of discussion questions and activities, aimed at younger readers, that could be used for common reads in a book club or classroom. At the time it was published, the novel garnered a number of prestigious accolades from the likes of the American Library Assn., the International Reading Assn., etc. For once, I think it deserved every critical recognition it got (and I don't often agree with the critical community!).<br /><br />"You may wish me luck, or curse me for a damnable pirate," Nancy writes near the close of her account. This reader opted for the first choice, without apology!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10728138717870437961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_333918141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333918141" />
    <a title="Emi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9670886-emi"><img alt="Emi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395539940p2/9670886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333918141?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emi" href="/user/show/9670886-emi">Emi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333918141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13621053836570454381">Someone commented that the writing was weird and confusing. I don't find it confusing at all. I will admit listening to it on audio book might help with that, as I did the first time around. But this time I read it. We have the story of a girl who wants to be rebellious in a world that sees her a currency for land and wealth. She lives innocently and oblivious to the schemes of the men around her until one day she takes action against a man trying to hurt her best friend. They run away and becom</span>
  <span id="freeText13621053836570454381" style="display:none">Someone commented that the writing was weird and confusing. I don't find it confusing at all. I will admit listening to it on audio book might help with that, as I did the first time around. But this time I read it. We have the story of a girl who wants to be rebellious in a world that sees her a currency for land and wealth. She lives innocently and oblivious to the schemes of the men around her until one day she takes action against a man trying to hurt her best friend. They run away and become pirates to escape their lives on Jamaica. <br /><br />Someone also commented that she didn't grow as a character but that also isn't true. She went from being a girl who did what she was told and went where she was told to standing for what she believes in, in her own weird-for-her-time way. She thinks of others before herself in a different way now as well. <br /><br />This story was breathtaking. I was riveted and couldn't put it down until I was done. Yes there were parts like in any other book that you think wow can we move on, but it's nothing more than a paragraph that I felt like this and not very often. It is juvenile fiction but the story should captivate anyone and doesn't read as simple as most juvenile fiction.<br /><br />Read: August 2005, May 2012</span>

<div id="review_21042957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21042957" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/750890-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199682849p2/750890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21042957?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/750890-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21042957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8301254025557116217">A young adult novel that I read exclusively because the teens in my book group had a serious hard-on for the Pirates of the Carribean movies. It’s a good story that seems backgrounded well with research, and it’s a quick read about two teenage girls -- one an English heiress, the other her slave -- who become pirates. It doesn’t gloss over what a pirate’s life entailed, but it refuses to linger on the more unsavory aspects of it, choosing to go a more light-hearted route. Considering that Rees’ </span>
  <span id="freeText8301254025557116217" style="display:none">A young adult novel that I read exclusively because the teens in my book group had a serious hard-on for the Pirates of the Carribean movies. It’s a good story that seems backgrounded well with research, and it’s a quick read about two teenage girls -- one an English heiress, the other her slave -- who become pirates. It doesn’t gloss over what a pirate’s life entailed, but it refuses to linger on the more unsavory aspects of it, choosing to go a more light-hearted route. Considering that Rees’ main goal is to entertain (and capitalize on the current pop culture hunger for all things of a piratical nature), that’s fair enough. You can’t take a book with an exclamation point in the title too seriously anyway.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8301254025557116217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3500285121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3500285121" />
    <a title="Aoife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife"><img alt="Aoife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514771423p2/16768476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3500285121?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife">Aoife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408800270" href="/book/show/4965146-pirates">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=historic">historic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=femalefriendship">femalefriendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=pretty-damn-good">pretty-damn-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=my-bookshelf">my-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=gryffindor">gryffindor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=childhood-favourite">childhood-favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3500285121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4103021571018497284">Nancy Kingston is in for a shock when her beloved father dies, and she travels to his plantation in the West Indies with her brother, leaving her childhood friend and betrothed behind. When arriving at the plantation, Nancy is shocked to discover her father was a keeper of slaves and her brother is attempting to marry her off to a cruel neighbor. Nancy and Minerva, a girl she befriends on the plantation, run away together and end up boarding a pirate ship in disguise, and start their life as hig</span>
  <span id="freeText4103021571018497284" style="display:none">Nancy Kingston is in for a shock when her beloved father dies, and she travels to his plantation in the West Indies with her brother, leaving her childhood friend and betrothed behind. When arriving at the plantation, Nancy is shocked to discover her father was a keeper of slaves and her brother is attempting to marry her off to a cruel neighbor. Nancy and Minerva, a girl she befriends on the plantation, run away together and end up boarding a pirate ship in disguise, and start their life as high sea adventurers.<br /><br />This book always gets 5/5 stars for me on the nostalgia level because I frickin loved this book as a young girl, and I still remember the thrills from when I initially read it, and marveled at this amazing, exciting life of female pirates.<br /><br />Celia Rees expertly combines a story of two women who are struggling to find different kinds of freedom - Minerva freedom to be herself without suffering cruelty and racism, and Nancy a freedom to be herself away from the bindings of society. The friendship and sisterly bond between Nancy and Minerva is everything, and it is the main focal point of the story for me and romantic relationships are completely overshadowed by Nancy's love for Minerva which is fantastic.<br /><br />While Celia Rees doesn't shy away from the cruelty and injustice of the time period - particularly the treatment of people of colour and the disgusting slave trade, there's definitely a sense of acceptance the older reader needs to have with the adventures Nancy and Minerva have as female pirates and the level of safety they appeared to have on board the ship, and the lack of injuries they obtained while fighting.<br /><br />The book does slow down a bit near the middle, and the pace meanders for a while before picking back up, and the resolution and the ending of the 'villain' near the end all happens a little bit quickly. <br /><br />But I absolutely love this book. Some amazing, strong female characters fighting for their right to be exactly who they are and I adore it. 100% recommend to everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4103021571018497284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107812538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107812538" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1884715-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235423776p2/1884715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107812538?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/1884715-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107812538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13991993296108250986">Although I was fully prepared to like this book, (I love seafaring stories), the book didn't hold up to my expectations (fixed high by the likes of London, Stevenson, Jacques and Luke). There is a wealth of potential, with good characters and conflicts, exotic settings, and a sense of historically accurate details, but the narration is slow: with full details of events that bring little interest, and skimming quickly over the most important climactic action. The reading is easy, but it is too cl</span>
  <span id="freeText13991993296108250986" style="display:none">Although I was fully prepared to like this book, (I love seafaring stories), the book didn't hold up to my expectations (fixed high by the likes of London, Stevenson, Jacques and Luke). There is a wealth of potential, with good characters and conflicts, exotic settings, and a sense of historically accurate details, but the narration is slow: with full details of events that bring little interest, and skimming quickly over the most important climactic action. The reading is easy, but it is too clean cut. The protagonists face danger after danger, but there is never a sense of risk. The reader is allowed to take for granted that no character of importance will be harmed. Almost every detail in the long train of events is impossibly contrived, so that there is no real excitement. The underlying drama that drives the story is the romance between Nancy and her lover William, but in the end this storyline takes a backseat, and is never concluded. <br />In the beginning, I noticed a strong resemblance to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/310146.The_True_Confessions_of_Charlotte_Doyle" title="The True Confessions of Charlotte Doyle by Avi" rel="nofollow noopener">The True Confessions of Charlotte Doyle</a> by avi, but avi's story was more complex, with greater risk, elevated danger, and plot twists. Pirates! was predictable and unalterably safe - not what I expect or want from such a title. So if perilous adventure on the high seas be what ye desire, put down "Pirates!" and take up instead the pages of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/310146.The_True_Confessions_of_Charlotte_Doyle" title="The True Confessions of Charlotte Doyle by Avi" rel="nofollow noopener">The True Confessions of Charlotte Doyle</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43049.The_Sea_Wolf" title="The Sea Wolf by Jack London" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sea Wolf</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/295.Treasure_Island" title="Treasure Island by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Treasure Island</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7980.Pearls_of_Lutra__Redwall___9_" title="Pearls of Lutra (Redwall, #9) by Brian Jacques" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pearls of Lutra</a>, or heck, even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/178629.Benito_Cereno" title="Benito Cereno by Herman Melville" rel="nofollow noopener">Benito Cereno</a>. Any one of these will be better reading, and more challenging for the mind. (I know "Benito Cereno" is a difficult read, but it has more twists and suspense in its few pages than "Pirates!" can shake a stick at!)<br />But whatever it lacked in excitement, it made up for in success. Those pirates got more loot with less trouble and in less time than any I've ever heard of!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13991993296108250986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_9587049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9587049" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/634508-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1198221874p2/634508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9587049?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/634508-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/634508-kathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/634508-kathy?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/634508-kathy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9587049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1261870284419777923">Nancy Kingdon is the daughter of a rich merchant. When her father’s fleet is lost in a terrible storm, he makes a bargain with a man known as The Brazilian. Nancy is unaware that her father has promised her hand in marriage to this man in exchange for gold. When her father dies suddenly, her brothers send her to her father’s plantation in Jamaica. She lives there for a time, unaware that she will soon be presented to The Brazilian, who lives on a neighboring plantation. Nancy and her house slave</span>
  <span id="freeText1261870284419777923" style="display:none">Nancy Kingdon is the daughter of a rich merchant. When her father’s fleet is lost in a terrible storm, he makes a bargain with a man known as The Brazilian. Nancy is unaware that her father has promised her hand in marriage to this man in exchange for gold. When her father dies suddenly, her brothers send her to her father’s plantation in Jamaica. She lives there for a time, unaware that she will soon be presented to The Brazilian, who lives on a neighboring plantation. Nancy and her house slave, Minerva, become fast friends. When Nancy’s fate becomes clear to her, she runs away and Minerva joins her. The two girls fall in with a band of pirates, dress as men, join the crew, and set off on the adventure of a lifetime.<br /><br />Reaction: I’ve always loved pirates and thoroughly enjoyed this tale of female pirates on the high seas. The story is set at the beginning of the 18th century and Rees does a good job of illustrating the historical backdrop. The reader learns something of the rum and slave trade of that time period as well as interesting pirate facts. Some of the story borders on the unbelievable, but what good pirate yarn doesn’t? Also, this is a nice title for female young adult readers who don’t want to leave the swashbuckling all to the guys.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1261870284419777923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_190379121" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190379121" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5881528-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372581064p2/5881528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190379121?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/5881528-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190379121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11800716390201684549">Perhaps it is because I am an adult and this book was written for a younger audience, but I was not impressed by this book at all! When you read the back of the book, the plot seems exciting and fast paced. This is not the case when you actually begin to read the book. The plot moves slowly, and Celia Rees has a HEAVY hand with foreshadowing. She tells her reader every twist and turn before it happens. This completely ruined the book for me. I also couldn't develop an attachment to either of the</span>
  <span id="freeText11800716390201684549" style="display:none">Perhaps it is because I am an adult and this book was written for a younger audience, but I was not impressed by this book at all! When you read the back of the book, the plot seems exciting and fast paced. This is not the case when you actually begin to read the book. The plot moves slowly, and Celia Rees has a HEAVY hand with foreshadowing. She tells her reader every twist and turn before it happens. This completely ruined the book for me. I also couldn't develop an attachment to either of the main characters. Both Nancy and Minerva are poorly developed and the reason why Nancy and Minerva are such close friends is poorly explained. Nancy is fairly whiny and helpless for a pirate. It also seemed like Celia Rees forgot about the antagoist (the Brazilian) at points in the book. It seemed rather unbelievable to me that Nancy was able to have prophetic dreams about the Brazilian, and that he was able to track her movements through the rubies he gave her. If you don't require much from your literature, go ahead and read this mess. But if you enjoy well-written novels, I would recommend looking for a different book to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11800716390201684549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I love pirate stories, and was satisfied that there was a good amount of swashbuckling at times. The majority of the book was kind of boring, though. I really didn't like the main character, but I did like Minerva and all her badassery. Minerva's mom was probably my favorite character.   <span id="freeText1527875180790004033" style="display:none">I did enjoy this one, though I probably won't reread it. I love pirate stories, and was satisfied that there was a good amount of swashbuckling at times. The majority of the book was kind of boring, though. I really didn't like the main character, but I did like Minerva and all her badassery. Minerva's mom was probably my favorite character. She was so strong in the face of adversity and abuse and did everything she could for her daughter. She was a great mother figure for Nancy, too. The villain, Nancy's horrible fiancé, almost had me gagging. Every time he showed up in the story, I just got the chills. He's a total creep. I also found that the tone of the story was so bleak throughout. There were barely any remotely happy moments in the book until the very end, but I felt so disconnected from most of the characters that I found myself not really caring all that much. All in all, it's a decent read if you're into historical fiction and pirates, like I am.</span>

<div id="review_2813479083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813479083" />
    <a title="Celia Buell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29892659-celia-buell"><img alt="Celia Buell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550789566p2/29892659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813479083?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celia Buell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celia Buell" href="/user/show/29892659-celia-buell">Celia Buell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=colonization">colonization</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=culture-exchange">culture-exchange</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=multicultural">multicultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=loss">loss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=overcoming-adversity">overcoming-adversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813479083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16074315522695181233">I'm sad to say that I didn't enjoy <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/143727.Pirates_' title='Pirates! by Celia Rees' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pirates!</a> as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83085.Celia_Rees' title='Celia Rees' rel='nofollow noopener'>Celia Rees</a>'s previous novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_' title='Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees' rel='nofollow noopener'>Witch Child</a>. While I loved the premise behind the story - two girls who run away from oppression and slavery and join with pirates in the 1700s - I just didn't feel like there was enough action and conflict to make a good adventure story. <br/><br/>When there was action, it seemed forced, and it was always between long periods of nothingness. There were not a lot of interpersonal conflict, and although Nancy is fighting a </span>
  <span id="freeText16074315522695181233" style="display:none">I'm sad to say that I didn't enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/143727.Pirates_" title="Pirates! by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Pirates!</a> as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83085.Celia_Rees" title="Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Celia Rees</a>'s previous novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a>. While I loved the premise behind the story - two girls who run away from oppression and slavery and join with pirates in the 1700s - I just didn't feel like there was enough action and conflict to make a good adventure story. <br /><br />When there was action, it seemed forced, and it was always between long periods of nothingness. There were not a lot of interpersonal conflict, and although Nancy is fighting a lot of internal conflict, it was always the same and never played up enough.<br /><br />I also feel as if the main villain, Bartholome, was not played up nearly enough. Why was he <i>so</i> set on marrying Nancy that he would stop everything to hunt her down? What were his plans originally? Why was Phillis convinced he was going to kill Nancy? Did he have power of his own, or was he given it from somewhere? Where did he get his cursed rubies from? All we really know is that he's Bartholome the evil Brazilian, and that really wasn't enough to go off of.<br /><br />The same way his character lacked any story or substance, so, in many ways, did the main protagonist, Nancy Kington's. Nancy just doesn't seem to grow as a character. She always has to overcome the same fears, whether it's knowing Bartholome is hunting her or leaving Minerva. Throughout the novel, she deals with everything the exact same way, and she doesn't really change her mindset at all either.<br /><br />None of the other characters are given much of a story either, even as we get to know them throughout the novel. None of them seem to have histories, and none of them are the types that a reader would care about after the story is finished. They just kind of exist within the novel but not outside its pages.<br /><br />This is in stark contrast to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a>, where there doesn't seem to be a lot of character development at first, but by the end you realize that each character had a very important role, and you want to know more about the characters and their lives. Here, everyone is just flat.<br /><br />Because I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a> so much, and because I have every intention of enjoying an author who shares my name, I think that made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/143727.Pirates_" title="Pirates! by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Pirates!</a> even more of a disappointment in a lot of ways. I do think, however, that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83085.Celia_Rees" title="Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Celia Rees</a> does have a lot of potential and writes in a way that I do like a lot. I'd love to explore more of her books and see where I rate them, and I will probably start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/493495.Soul_Taker" title="Soul Taker by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Soul Taker</a>, as I have a physical copy of it. I might also go with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/300017.Sorceress__Witch_Child___2_" title="Sorceress (Witch Child, #2) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorceress</a>, the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a>, as I really do want to find out what happened after Mary's story ends. Either way, it is not likely that I will reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/143727.Pirates_" title="Pirates! by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Pirates!</a> any time soon, or at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16074315522695181233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_82587726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82587726" />
    <a title="Amanda Bynum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/166315-amanda-bynum"><img alt="Amanda Bynum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183381835p2/166315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82587726?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Bynum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Bynum" href="/user/show/166315-amanda-bynum">Amanda Bynum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82587726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7324990348947928249">I kicked off my Cannonball Read endeavor with Pirates!, a young adult novel on girl pirates in the 18th century. It was a solid way to start the project - relatively short, somewhat frivolous, lesbian overtones, and only a couple mentions of scurvy (but no scurvy dogs). Nancy is fleeing an arranged marriage; Minerva, a life of slavery. They join up with a band of pirates, and yes, blood is shed, but hearts are also led to love. Like I said, girl pirates. They don't make out or anything, but they</span>
  <span id="freeText7324990348947928249" style="display:none">I kicked off my Cannonball Read endeavor with Pirates!, a young adult novel on girl pirates in the 18th century. It was a solid way to start the project - relatively short, somewhat frivolous, lesbian overtones, and only a couple mentions of scurvy (but no scurvy dogs). Nancy is fleeing an arranged marriage; Minerva, a life of slavery. They join up with a band of pirates, and yes, blood is shed, but hearts are also led to love. Like I said, girl pirates. They don't make out or anything, but they do bathe each other a couple times. It was fun, not too brain-taxing, and I enjoyed it.<br /><br /><br />I wonder why Celia Rees felt the need to put an exclamation point in the title of her book. Is Pirates! any better than Pirates? Would readers not understand that book is in fact about pirates if the exclamation point were not presents? Then I got to wondering: what would the titles of other solid literary works be like if they too were punctuated so emphatically?<br />Brothers!<br />Geisha!<br />Jane! (take your pick)<br />Atonement!<br /><br /><br />Pirates! - B+</span>
  <a data-text-id="7324990348947928249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112912364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14105033518173571627">This story of two teenaged girls who choose to become pirates because of the desperateness of their lives is, as it claims to be, pretty exciting. When Nancy Kington's father dies soon after his shipping business is devastated by a storm (and his son's drinking and gambling addictions), it is expected that Nancy will solve the family's financial problems by marrying the wealthy, but mysterious and evil Bartholome. Despite her opposition to this plan, she isn't driven to join with pirates until s</span>
  <span id="freeText14105033518173571627" style="display:none">This story of two teenaged girls who choose to become pirates because of the desperateness of their lives is, as it claims to be, pretty exciting. When Nancy Kington's father dies soon after his shipping business is devastated by a storm (and his son's drinking and gambling addictions), it is expected that Nancy will solve the family's financial problems by marrying the wealthy, but mysterious and evil Bartholome. Despite her opposition to this plan, she isn't driven to join with pirates until she kills her plantation's overseer to prevent him from raping Minerva, one of her slaves. This is a pirate story in which the violence and gore are not much softened. Slave conditions, amputations, duelling and other fighting and shipboard injuries are explicitly depicted. Additionally, other prevalent vices (drinking, gambling, whoring) are an integral part of the story - though not explicitly described. It may seem slow starting, but if they stick with it, readers will find so much action, they may not realize that they are getting history as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14105033518173571627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11116529760454441736">Pirates! By Celia Rees is a good YA melodrama Nancy Kington about 1700 is the young daughter of a Bristol merchant, somewhat similar to the Bloody Jack series by <br/>L.A. Meyer this is a bit more serious and though it’s not a series or a dozen or more novels this is good historical fiction with some Bad language of the d-word sort present but relatively restrained, rape or attempted rape and prostitution are part of this world but not portrayed in great detail, and while there are some very violent </span>
  <span id="freeText11116529760454441736" style="display:none">Pirates! By Celia Rees is a good YA melodrama Nancy Kington about 1700 is the young daughter of a Bristol merchant, somewhat similar to the Bloody Jack series by <br />L.A. Meyer this is a bit more serious and though it’s not a series or a dozen or more novels this is good historical fiction with some Bad language of the d-word sort present but relatively restrained, rape or attempted rape and prostitution are part of this world but not portrayed in great detail, and while there are some very violent and grisly moments, Rees doesn’t wallow in them. Ms. Kingston who has now inherited the family Fountainhead plantation in Jamaica after the death of her father<br />is horrified when she sees how the family fortune has been built on the scarred backs of black people. She takes an immediate dislike to the family's cruel overseer and befriends two house slaves, Phyllis Sharpe and her daughter Minerva. Many surprises and twists and turns follow including her being forced to become a outlaw and a pirate. Written kind of for the YA market it still works for older readers I enjoyed it it was a fun book four stars overall. <br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_937007730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937007730" />
    <a title="Evan Baldonado" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23186550-evan-baldonado"><img alt="Evan Baldonado" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506192173p2/23186550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/937007730?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan Baldonado" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan Baldonado" href="/user/show/23186550-evan-baldonado">Evan Baldonado</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937007730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4074982056950021193">Review<br/><br/>⅘ stars! Overall, I was pleasantly surprised by Pirates!. I usually only read dystopians, so I didn’t really know what to expect. This book probably worked out well for me because there was lots of adventure and action. I also really enjoyed was the usage of maritime terms such as ‘schooner’ and ‘topsail’. One thing that I didn’t like was the excessive amount of foreshadowing that Celia Rees used. She used it every chapter or so. Overall, I would recommend this book for middle-schoolers be</span>
  <span id="freeText4074982056950021193" style="display:none">Review<br /><br />⅘ stars! Overall, I was pleasantly surprised by Pirates!. I usually only read dystopians, so I didn’t really know what to expect. This book probably worked out well for me because there was lots of adventure and action. I also really enjoyed was the usage of maritime terms such as ‘schooner’ and ‘topsail’. One thing that I didn’t like was the excessive amount of foreshadowing that Celia Rees used. She used it every chapter or so. Overall, I would recommend this book for middle-schoolers because it contains a bit of strong language and some mature concepts.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Summary<br /><br />It is the year 1722 and sixteen-year-old Nancy Kington is sent to her family’s sugar plantation in Jamaica after her father’s death. Nancy is going to be married to a Brazilian man by the name of Bartholome. She is very upset as she has plans to marry William, her childhood friend who is now a marine. However, she and her new friend, Minerva Sharpe, a slave on her plantation, escape just in time. Bartholome is after them and the chase is on. They hide with the Maroons, escaped slaves. But, they fear that their presence is endangering them, so they leave with pirates, led by Captain Broom. They then attack other ships for awhile and Minerva confides in Nancy that they are actually blood sisters because they have the same dad. According to section eight of the Articles (the rules of the ship), “No man is to talk of breaking up our way of living until each has been shared £1000. If any man lose a limb, or become crippled in our service, he shall have the sum of £150, and shall remain with the company as long as he shall think fit.” They end up parting ways in New York, each receiving more than £1000. However, many people come back and they leave New York for more adventures, as Bartholome’s ship is right outside the harbor. They swap their three-masted ship for a much faster schooner called Swift Return. But, They encounter a storm and have to go to Nassau harbor. While they are restocking their supplies and trading, the Navy comes into get them, headed by William. This is an awful turn of events for Nancy, as she never wanted William to see her a Pirate. However, William doesn't recognize her because she is disguised as a man. On the Navy ship, Nancy and Minerva manage to get alone with William, but the chase for the rest of the Swift Return’s crew is still on. When chasing them along the shoreline, the Navy ship’s anchors fail to gain purchase and Nancy and Minerva end up on a deserted island after the ship breaks. There, they are picked up by the Swift Return. Captain Broom decides that raiding merchant ships isn't good enough and that they want gold. So, they leave for Africa and raid a base there. On their way back, however, they are found by Bartholome. Minerva ends up killing him and everyone lives happily ever after. Minerva and Vincent, her sailor friend get married, and Nancy goes off to look for William, her childhood love.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4074982056950021193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_839046460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839046460" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5388214-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528799424p2/5388214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839046460?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/5388214-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408800270" href="/book/show/4965146-pirates">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5388214-sophie?shelf=ya-teenage-books">ya-teenage-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839046460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17384740796754638281">This book wins most of its stars for strong characters, beautiful writing and interesting historical details. The plot, however, was a bit of a disappointment.<br/><br/><i>Pirates!</i>, or to give it its full title, <i>Pirates! - The true and remarkable adventures of Minerva Sharpe and Nancy Kington, Female Pyrates</i>, is the story of two girls who escape their very different 17th century lives to live a life of piracy. Nancy is a rich girl from Bristol who goes to live on her father's plantation after his death and i</span>
  <span id="freeText17384740796754638281" style="display:none">This book wins most of its stars for strong characters, beautiful writing and interesting historical details. The plot, however, was a bit of a disappointment.<br /><br /><i>Pirates!</i>, or to give it its full title, <i>Pirates! - The true and remarkable adventures of Minerva Sharpe and Nancy Kington, Female Pyrates</i>, is the story of two girls who escape their very different 17th century lives to live a life of piracy. Nancy is a rich girl from Bristol who goes to live on her father's plantation after his death and is sold into a forced marriage, while Minerva is a slave on the plantation. It felt like Minerva had the most interesting story, and she is certainly featured prominently on the cover and in the title, yet Nancy is the main character, strangely.<br /><br />Unlike Celia Rees' other books that I've read (<i>Witch Child</i> and <i>Sorceress</i>), the plot felt quite lacking in real peril and although there was a lot of conflict, it was always diffused in a few pages. I felt that the things that happened to the slaves on the plantation were by far the worst, making everything else seem rather trivial.<br /><br />The main character's romance feels very forced given that she's in love with someone who she only has a couple of brief conversations with. I thought that there was a romantic subtext between the two girls for most of the book until <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the author revealed they were actually half-sisters <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which made me feel pretty strange! There are also some supernatural elements which I didn't feel really worked in a story that was trying to be so realistic. <br /><br />The ending is fairly satisfying (though a little rushed), but it doesn't really tie up all of the loose ends. It seems from the author's website that there was meant to be a sequel to this book, which would explain that. You can read an extract here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.celiarees.com/books/pirates.html">http://www.celiarees.com/books/pirate...</a> <br /><br /><i>Pirates!</i> is a decent read for anyone who likes historical YA fiction and immersing themselves in the past. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17384740796754638281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1201962285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1201962285" />
    <a title="lostinabookbrb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2881826-lostinabookbrb"><img alt="lostinabookbrb" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1201962285?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lostinabookbrb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lostinabookbrb" href="/user/show/2881826-lostinabookbrb">lostinabookbrb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1201962285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15095805935105249579">I bought this book wanting to love it. It’s about pirates who so happen to be women. I was also hoping this would lead to pirates who so happen to be women and gay. Why was I hoping for this? Because it would have been interesting and different from a lot of other female pirate books. <br/><br/>Well, as it were, there are no female gay pirates. Instead, there is a gal who wants to be with her childhood friend, William, and is instead put into an arranged marriage with this guy who is known throughout the </span>
  <span id="freeText15095805935105249579" style="display:none">I bought this book wanting to love it. It’s about pirates who so happen to be women. I was also hoping this would lead to pirates who so happen to be women and gay. Why was I hoping for this? Because it would have been interesting and different from a lot of other female pirate books. <br /><br />Well, as it were, there are no female gay pirates. Instead, there is a gal who wants to be with her childhood friend, William, and is instead put into an arranged marriage with this guy who is known throughout the book as the Brazilian. (There’s also a point where she kills a guy who tries to rape this gal who is a slave on the plantation her father owned). <br /><br />AT ANY RATE! All that sounds like an interesting plot and it is an interesting plot. However, it fails to live up to its potential. <br /><br />Celia has a bad habit throughout the book of telling and not showing.<br /><br />For example, there is a scene where the pirates argue whether they should allow women onto their ship. We are told it is a very tense moment with a rousing speech from the captain but we’re not shown. There’s no scene really set and we don’t even get to know what the Captain said to get his crew to agree.<br /><br />This happens throughout the novel. <br /><br />There’s also this Brazilian fellow. He is featured at the beginning of the story for a brief period and a bit towards the end. While he is definitely not someone Nancy or any sane woman would want to marry, it is hard to understand Nancy’s fear when he isn’t really seen or heard from again until the last 60 pages of the novel. We’re told he is following her but there are no close calls until he catches up to them at the end.<br /><br />It’s a book that decided to tell us there was conflict and awesome battle scenes without actually showing them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15095805935105249579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_137295172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137295172" />
    <a title="Karissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa"><img alt="Karissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557318686p2/4057501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137295172?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137295172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3422083130529530664">I picked up this book because I had be seeing it on shelves for ages and was curious. It ended up being a pretty darn good book.<br/><br/>This book tells the story of a young girl, Nancy, who is the daughter to a sugar plantation owner. When Nancy's father dies. Nancy is spirited away by her brothers to live on their sugar plantation in Jamaica. Upon her arrival she finds that she has been promised to a horrible man for marriage. Certain circumstances come about and Nancy ends up fleeing for her life and </span>
  <span id="freeText3422083130529530664" style="display:none">I picked up this book because I had be seeing it on shelves for ages and was curious. It ended up being a pretty darn good book.<br /><br />This book tells the story of a young girl, Nancy, who is the daughter to a sugar plantation owner. When Nancy's father dies. Nancy is spirited away by her brothers to live on their sugar plantation in Jamaica. Upon her arrival she finds that she has been promised to a horrible man for marriage. Certain circumstances come about and Nancy ends up fleeing for her life and signing up to be serve as a pirate on a pirate ship. The majority of the book is spent on her adventures.<br /><br />This was a very good book. The writing style is very straight forward, the whole book is from Nancy's perspective. The plot moves slowly at the beginning with the the first third of the book telling about how Nancy and Minerva got onto the pirate ship. The pace picks up from there and hurtles from adventure to adventure. It was a thoroughly enjoyable read.<br /><br />I have one small complaint about the book and that was that it dealt with pirates from a very romantic point of view; the violence of a pirate's lifestyle is somewhat muted. I think young girls would have been hard pressed to serve as women on a pirate ship in reality. Of course, this isn't reality, it's just a very good story that definitely sways toward fantasy. It reminded me a lot of the Pirates of the Caribbean movie. It is a very solid young adult novel.<br /><br />I liked the book and will be checking out more books by this author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3422083130529530664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('50Vkb5UmYqb9AH2y4hFDGVJo95mOzQ67e7KpO0Hz271fwW4YU3YcUvkwAnLrs6VvzC6rdslXXazYfbfw85zaIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+qxOuJou0KRbeBoFMvdQrYL2yx+ieE02nh9dkESB5WhCKETPXH6uUF9IZcU7VbbbHLCX8OXiHiE90ENb9u7k9A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14871513440215808737">Celia Rees (born 1949) is an English author of children's, YA and Adult fiction. <br/><br/>She was born in 1949 in Solihull, West Midlands but now lives in Leamington Spa with her husband. Rees attended University of Warwick and earned a degree in History of Politics. After university, she taught English in Coventry secondary schools for seventeen years, during which time she began to write.<br/><br/>Since then, she </span>
  <span id="freeText14871513440215808737" style="display:none">Celia Rees (born 1949) is an English author of children's, YA and Adult fiction. <br /><br />She was born in 1949 in Solihull, West Midlands but now lives in Leamington Spa with her husband. Rees attended University of Warwick and earned a degree in History of Politics. After university, she taught English in Coventry secondary schools for seventeen years, during which time she began to write.<br /><br />Since then, she has written over twenty YA titles. Her books have been translated into 28 languages. She has been short listed for the Guardian, Whitbread (now Costa) and W.H. Smith Children’s Book Awards. She is a regular tutor for the Arvon Foundation. She has been Chair of the Children’s Writers and Illustrators Group and on the Society of Authors’ Management Committee.<br /><br />Her first book for adults, Miss Graham's Cold War Cookbook, was published by HarperCollins in July, 2020. <br /><br /></span>
